<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">E number</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the food additive codes. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/E_number_(disambiguation)" title="E number (disambiguation)">E number (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riboflavin_solution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1788" data-file-width="1497" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Riboflavin_solution.jpg/170px-Riboflavin_solution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Riboflavin_solution.jpg/255px-Riboflavin_solution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Riboflavin_solution.jpg/340px-Riboflavin_solution.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riboflavin_solution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A solution of E101 <a href="/wiki/Riboflavin" title="Riboflavin">riboflavin</a> (also known as vitamin B2)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2149" data-file-width="3228" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg/220px-Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg/330px-Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg/440px-Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monosodium_glutamate_crystals.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Crystals of E621 <a href="/wiki/Monosodium_glutamate" title="Monosodium glutamate">monosodium glutamate</a>, a flavour enhancer</div></div></div>
<p><b>E numbers</b> are codes for substances that are permitted to be used as <a href="/wiki/Food_additive" title="Food additive">food additives</a> for use within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a>. The "E" stands for "Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Commonly found on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_label" title="Food label">food labels</a>, their safety assessment and approval are the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/European_Food_Safety_Authority" title="European Food Safety Authority">European Food Safety Authority</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>Having a single unified list for food additives was first agreed upon in 1962 with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_colouring" title="Food colouring">food colouring</a>. In 1964, the directives for preservatives were added, 1970 for antioxidants and 1974 for the emulsifiers, stabilisers, thickeners and gelling agents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Numbering_schemes">Numbering schemes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=E_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Numbering schemes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The numbering scheme follows that of the <a href="/wiki/International_Numbering_System_for_Food_Additives" title="International Numbering System for Food Additives">International Numbering System</a> (INS) as determined by the <i><a href="/wiki/Codex_Alimentarius" title="Codex Alimentarius">Codex Alimentarius</a></i> committee<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncsi_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncsi-6">[6]</a></sup>, though only a subset of the INS additives are approved for use in the European Union as food additives. Outside the European continent plus Russia, E numbers are also encountered on food labelling in other jurisdictions, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf</a>, South Africa, Australia, New Zealand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>, Malaysia, and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. They are increasingly, though still rarely, found on North American packaging<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>, especially on imported European products.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colloquial_use">Colloquial use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=E_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colloquial use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In some European countries, "E number" is sometimes used informally as a pejorative term for artificial food additives, and products may promote themselves as "free of E numbers". This is incorrect, because many components of natural foods have assigned E numbers (and the number is a synonym for the chemical component), e.g. <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ascorbic_acid" title="Ascorbic acid">E300</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Lycopene" title="Lycopene">lycopene</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E160d" title="E160d">E160d</a>), found in <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a>.
</p>

<p>NB: Not all examples of a class fall into the given numeric range. Moreover, many chemicals, particularly in the E400–499 range, have a variety of purposes.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_list">Full list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=E_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Full list">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The list shows all components that have or had an E-number assigned. <i>Not all additives listed are still allowed in the EU</i>, but are listed as they used to have an E-number. For an overview of currently allowed additives see <a class="external text" href="http://www.food.gov.uk/safereating/chemsafe/additivesbranch/enumberlist" rel="nofollow">information provided by the Food Standards Agency of the UK</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=E_number&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="http://www.codexalimentarius.org" rel="nofollow">Codex Alimentarius</a>, the international foods standards, established by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO) in 1963
<ul><li>See also their document "<a class="external text" href="http://www.codexalimentarius.net/download/standards/7/CXG_036e.pdf" rel="nofollow">Class Names and the International Numbering System for Food Additives</a>" (Ref: CAC/GL #36 publ. 1989, revised 2009, amended 2011)</li></ul></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.who.int/foodsafety/chem/jecfa/publications/en/index.html" rel="nofollow">Joint FAO/WHO Expert Committee on Food Additives (JECFA) publications</a> at the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> (WHO)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.fao.org/ag/agn/jecfa-additives/index.html" rel="nofollow">Food Additive Index</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JECFA" title="JECFA">JECFA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.guidedways.com/halalfoodguide.php" rel="nofollow">E-codes and ingredients search engine with details/suggestions for Muslims</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/food/food/fAEF/additives/lists_authorised_fA_en.htm" rel="nofollow">Current EU approved additives and their E Numbers</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.foodlaw.rdg.ac.uk/additive.htm" rel="nofollow">Food Additives in the European Union</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/food/food/fAEF/additives/index_en.htm" rel="nofollow">Food Additives</a>, Food Safety, website of the European Union. Includes (a) Lists of authorised food additives (b) Food additives database</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.faia.org.uk/" rel="nofollow">The Food Additives and Ingredients Association, FAIA website, UK.</a></li></ul>
